  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e5393efc-1e5a-48b9-bed2-880ddf3eb174'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText14182149097183662831" style="display:none">When Olivia Villalobos finds a bloodstained love letter she endeavors to deliver it before Chief Inspector Sedeño finds it in her possession.<br /><br />A city along the southern coast of Puerto Rico emerges in the aftermath of the Spanish-American War. Olivia, daughter of a drunkard police investigator who never knew the truth behind her mother’s disappearance, finds a bloodstained love letter in the hidden compartment of her father’s coat. Convinced it belonged to the man recently found dead she sets out to deliver it to the Labyrinth of Love Letters. A mysterious place believed to be an urban legend where the transients of forbidden love leave missives for one another. She enlists the help of Isaac Quintero to find the Labyrinth and they soon realize their quest has opened the door into Old Sienna’s darkest secrets—the perils, madness and depth of tragic love</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1904393204" />
    <a title="Courtney" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19203783-courtney"><img alt="Courtney" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1454912500p2/19203783.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1904393204?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Courtney" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Courtney" href="/user/show/19203783-courtney">Courtney</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of : romance, crime mysteries, and historical fiction.</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Courtney by: </span>
      Booktasters
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19203783-courtney?shelf=2017-read">2017-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19203783-courtney?shelf=booktasters">booktasters</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1904393204" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4224179616077860005"><i>"The only thing worth living for, and dying for, is love."</i><br/><br/>Felix Alexander poetically blends together a well balanced mix of different genres that include: historical fiction, romance, and crime-mystery that are all tied together by urban legends, myths and faith. If you have a special bookish someone in your life, and are in need of any bookish gift ideas, then I suggest <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32978448.The_Last_Valentine' title='The Last Valentine by Felix Alexander' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Last Valentine</a>! It's publish date is on <u>Feb. 13th 2017</u> <b>(which is my birthday, yaaayy!)</b>, so it's perfect for this holiday! </span>
  <span id="freeText4224179616077860005" style="display:none"><i>"The only thing worth living for, and dying for, is love."</i><br /><br />Felix Alexander poetically blends together a well balanced mix of different genres that include: historical fiction, romance, and crime-mystery that are all tied together by urban legends, myths and faith. If you have a special bookish someone in your life, and are in need of any bookish gift ideas, then I suggest <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32978448.The_Last_Valentine" title="The Last Valentine by Felix Alexander" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Valentine</a>! It's publish date is on <u>Feb. 13th 2017</u> <b>(which is my birthday, yaaayy!)</b>, so it's perfect for this holiday! <br /><br />This story takes place in 1934, in a city called Old Sienna, located along the Southern coast of Puerto Rico. Olivia, the daughter of a drunkard police investigator (and our MC) discovers a blood stained letter in one of her father's coat pockets. Upon learning that the letter was written from a recently unidentified murder victim, to the woman he secretly loves, Olivia insists on delivering it to it's rightful place: the Labyrinth of Love Letter's. <br /><br />With the help of her long time childhood friend, Isaac Quintero, Olivia begins her search of this mysterious place, which is believed by many to only be an urban legend. Following any leads they're able to find, the pair uncover some of Old Sienna's darkest secrets, as well as some of those closest to them - <b>the perils, madness and depth of tragic love.</b> <br /><br />Filex Alexander writes about love as if he's been in it most of his life! He <i>beautifully</i> depicts emotions! His characters are fully developed and the world building is good. My only real complaint is that there are times when the author tends to give the reader a bunch lengthy paragraphs of info all at once. While the "info dumps" are useful and fun to read, they tend to take away from the story at times. The beginning of this book is slowly paced, but the story does pick up and the mystery grips you and sucks you in. <br /><br />This is a romance novel worth reading, especially if you have a love for Puerto Rico, romance, urban lengends and crime-mysteries.<br /><br /><br /><br /><b>**** I received an eBook copy of this title in exchange for an honest review. Thank you to Booktasters for introducing me to this author and thank you to Felix Alexander for giving Me the chance to read and review his novle. ****</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="4224179616077860005" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6843025647853697729">dnf @ 36% <br/><br/>i don't think i'm the right target audience for this... whereas i'm not averse to romantic books and relationships in novels, the whole idea of this was... dying for love, living for love, doing everything for love... all the plot surrounded that basic idea, and that is Not My Thing at all. i'm not rating it because i don't think it was objectively bad, it was just not my cup of tea. </span>

<div id="review_2048072762" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2048072762" />
    <a title="Bella James" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65006957-bella-james"><img alt="Bella James" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582291967p2/65006957.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2048072762?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bella James" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bella James" href="/user/show/65006957-bella-james">Bella James</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2048072762" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12022265838410684025">The Last Valentine, Felix Alexander.<br/><br/>Alexander's beautiful narrative is dark at times, but truly one for the Romantics. He captures the grip and agony of love, carefully threading each twist and turn of an elaborate plot, while creating intensely relatable characters.<br/>An intricate blend of mystery, romance and history, I particularly liked the metaphysical dynamic in relation to love after death.<br/><br/>In addition to the well thought out story line, this novel is seductively set along the south coast of </span>
  <span id="freeText12022265838410684025" style="display:none">The Last Valentine, Felix Alexander.<br /><br />Alexander's beautiful narrative is dark at times, but truly one for the Romantics. He captures the grip and agony of love, carefully threading each twist and turn of an elaborate plot, while creating intensely relatable characters.<br />An intricate blend of mystery, romance and history, I particularly liked the metaphysical dynamic in relation to love after death.<br /><br />In addition to the well thought out story line, this novel is seductively set along the south coast of Puerto Rico, during the aftermath of the Spanish-American war. The turbulent time in history seems to reflect the opening of the Pandora's Box that becomes apparent when secrets are revealed within The Labyrinth of Love Letters. We have darkness and light merging, along with the concept of love and loss. Angry and unrequited love are offset by a gentler unveiling of the unconditional love which transcends death. A truly remarkable read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12022265838410684025" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1845744336" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1845744336" />
    <a title="Proudtobebookish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14893046-proudtobebookish"><img alt="Proudtobebookish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1497254904p2/14893046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1845744336?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Proudtobebookish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Proudtobebookish" href="/user/show/14893046-proudtobebookish">Proudtobebookish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1845744336" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13591027152422873806">First of all I want to tell you that this review was wrote by me who use English as my second language <br/><br/> <b> 3 / 5 Stars of The Last Valentine by Felix Alexander </b><br/><br/>I scrolled through my twitter timeline for my next reading books recommendation a few weeks ago. And I stumbled upon this intriguing mystery novel by an indie author, Felix Alexander. If you follow me, you must know that I am a hopeless romance reader to the core. But for the past 8 months I extended my area of reading including nonfiction,</span>
  <span id="freeText13591027152422873806" style="display:none">First of all I want to tell you that this review was wrote by me who use English as my second language <br /><br /> <b> 3 / 5 Stars of The Last Valentine by Felix Alexander </b><br /><br />I scrolled through my twitter timeline for my next reading books recommendation a few weeks ago. And I stumbled upon this intriguing mystery novel by an indie author, Felix Alexander. If you follow me, you must know that I am a hopeless romance reader to the core. But for the past 8 months I extended my area of reading including nonfiction, classic, memoir, mystery and other genres (you can look at my other reviews to get a better idea). That’s why when I read The Last Valentine’s synopsis, I got the vibe this novel would help me make my scope of reading all more richer.<br /><br />The Last Valentine is set in Old Sienna, Puerto Rico in 1935. I knew next to nothing about Old Sienna and thus the premise became all the more intriguing. I ended up googling and gathering all sorts of pictures and information on Old Sienna, Puerto Rico, 1935 just to help myself get immerged within the story. <br />The story started off with a murder case and the chief police inspector found love letters as the only leading evidence. Unfortunately, he lost that piece of evidence and this is where the story grows more intense and more puzzles to introduced which are later solved. Truthfully, I was so mesmerized by the story during 26% progress of my reading because I desired to know what happened and how this case was linked to every character. <br />This book brought up very fascinating topics about love and marriage up and how things were in 1935. The purpose of marriage was to form alliances and secure family’s future, not the notion of love. This situation made unequal social layer where love even if it was true love was categorized as forbidden love. <br />The author’s writing style is almost lyrical, melodic and rich in vocabulary. The writing enhanced the beauty of these stories including the vivid sceneries that the author managed to paint within this novel with words alone. I cannot seem to make up my mind with the conclusion if The Last Valentine is a mystery novel with romance as an adding ingredient or vice versa even after I finished the book. <br /><br /><i>“The day waits for the sunrise and the night waits for sunset. This is how I wait for you, without regard for time, because I know you will return to me when you are ready” </i><br /><br /><i>“The longing in a stolen glance, the confession lingering on his lips, and the agony of unfulfilled desire swirling in his heart, like a breeze on a deserted mountainside. At that moment, he realized another shared his pain.”</i><br /><br /><i>“Love is the only memory one never loses, because even if one loses his mind the memory always remains in the heart”</i><br /><br />Other facts that I love from this book are every characters who stand out in their own beautiful uniqueness. Each of them has their own insight about love based on their own history. They all oblivious to the fact that all those loves eventually link them together. There was one mythical character that I was oh so fond of. Every time he showed up even for only a couple of scene, it got me in creepy but curios mode. I won’t give you any spoilers or hints, but this character somehow managed to not only develop the story’s mystery and romance side of things but another genre hmmm… fantasy maybe? Hehehe<br /><br /><b> Now the big question, why did I gave 3 stars?</b><br /><br />First, I did praise the author in his rich vocabulary but English is my second language, it impacted enjoyment of the overall story and at times pulled me out of the story completely. There times where I literally had to stop myself from reaching for a dictionary in order to get better understanding. Every time I stumbled upon words which I hadn’t heard before, I had to open the dictionary only to resume reading a couple of line back to understand the whole thing. Furthermore, this book has less conversation, and most of the story is written in wordy paragraphs. Some of the paragraphs have grammatical error and missing punctuations. <br />So yeah, I hope you can imagine why this problem definitely slowed me down and annoyed me a lot because I could not fully take pleasure in reading The Last Valentine. Second, the slow pace of the story kind of interfered with my reading. I told in the first paragraph above that I enjoyed The Last Valentine during 26% progress (I realized that the beginning had been far more fast paced) and after that the story slowed considerably though the ending really got me in the feels. I had thought I knew the direction the novel was heading managed at 78% of reading though I never expected the coming ending we got. <br /><br />Overall, my instinct was right. This book made from reading richer not only in scope of genre matters but also in vocabulary. Thanks to Mr. Felix Alexander. I found poem on a whole new level. I still recommend this book to you guys who are not having any difficulty in English though. I do believe you will enjoy it even read it in just one sitting <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13591027152422873806" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2007499714?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Yvonne (It&#39;s All About Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Yvonne (It&#39;s All About Books)" href="/user/show/17970468-yvonne-it-s-all-about-books">Yvonne (It&#39;s All About Books)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2007499714" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6234757359459119869"><a href='https://melovebooks.files.wordpress.com/2017/05/brthelastvalentine.jpg' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1495725392i/22851153._SX540_.jpg' alt='' width='400' height='165' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><strong>Finished reading: May 24th 2017</strong><br/><a href='https://melovebooks.files.wordpress.com/2014/06/35.jpg' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433873952i/15152986.jpg' alt='' width='101' height='26' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><blockquote>
<br/>"In their infinite wisdom they fail to realize that love keeps us young after youth has passed and is the only memory worth remembering when the shadows of forgetfulness linger on the horizon of old age."<br/>
</blockquote><br/><strong>
  *** A copy of this book was kindly provided to me by Reading Alley in exchange for an honest review. Thank you! ***
</strong><br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[<a href='https://melovebooks.files.wordpress.com/2014/09/myrambles11.jpg' rel='nofollow noopener'><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433783179i/15142120.jpg' alt='myrambles1reviewqqq' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/></a><br/><br/>I love stories with a different setting so the fact that <strong>The Last Valentine</strong> is set in Puerto Rico was a big selling point</span></span>
  <span id="freeText6234757359459119869" style="display:none"><a href="https://melovebooks.files.wordpress.com/2017/05/brthelastvalentine.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1495725392i/22851153._SX540_.jpg" alt="" width="400" height="165" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><strong>Finished reading: May 24th 2017</strong><br><a href="https://melovebooks.files.wordpress.com/2014/06/35.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433873952i/15152986.jpg" alt="" width="101" height="26" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><blockquote>
<br>"In their infinite wisdom they fail to realize that love keeps us young after youth has passed and is the only memory worth remembering when the shadows of forgetfulness linger on the horizon of old age."<br>
</blockquote><br><strong>
  *** A copy of this book was kindly provided to me by Reading Alley in exchange for an honest review. Thank you! ***
</strong><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<a href="https://melovebooks.files.wordpress.com/2014/09/myrambles11.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433783179i/15142120.jpg" alt="myrambles1reviewqqq" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>I love stories with a different setting so the fact that <strong>The Last Valentine</strong> is set in Puerto Rico was a big selling point for me. Add the promise of the combination of a historical fiction and mystery read, and I just knew I had to read this story…And it has definitely turned out to be an enjoyable read. Both the 1930s setting in Puerto Rico and the whole mystery around the labyrinth of love letters stood out for me. The descriptions are well done and I found myself looking forward to discover more about both the characters and what would happen to them. The writing style is enjoyable and also very quotable. I loved the inclusion of various Spanish words in the prose; it made the story feel that much more authentic without slowing down the pace for those who don't understand the language. The main plot of trying to unravel the mysteries around the labyrinth is intertwined with various love stories, secrets and conspiracies that will keep you interested until the very end. I did feel the dose of forbidden love, love triangles and romance in general was a bit too high for me and some of the characters started to annoy me because of it, but that might just have been me not liking those elements in general in the first place. It's not just the romance between the characters though, because <strong>The Last Valentine</strong> also talks a lot about romance itself with the help of for example love letters, romance quotes etc. If you enjoy a well written romance novel with a dose of mystery and historical facts will probably enjoy it even better than I did!<br><br><a href="https://melovebooks.files.wordpress.com/2014/09/shortsummary11.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433783179i/15142121.jpg" alt="shortsummary1reviewqqq" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>Olivia Villalobos is the daughter of a drunkard police investigator and never knew the truth behind the disappearance of her mother. One day she finds a bloodstained love letter in the hidden compartment of her father's coat... she is convinced it belonged to the man recently found dead, and is determined to find the Labyrinth of Love Letters to deliver it before someone else takes it away. The labyrinth is believed to be an urban legend, but is that all there is to the mysterious place? Olivia starts her search with the help of her best friend Isaac Quintero and soon they realize they might find more than they were looking for...<br><br><a href="https://melovebooks.files.wordpress.com/2014/08/finalthoughts.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433783179i/15142122.jpg" alt="finalthoughtsreviewqqq" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br><strong>The Last Valentine</strong> isn't just another historical romance novel. The 1930s setting in Puerto Rico is without doubt well executed and helped set the right atmosphere, but it is the whole mystery around the Labyrinth of Love Letters and other secrets and conspiracies that will keep you intrigued until the very end. The dose of (sappy) romance cliches was a bit too high for me, but I did appreciate the many quotable references to romance in general. Romance fans will most likely love this story! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>
  <i>P.S. Find more of my reviews <a href="http://melovebooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.</i>

<div id="review_1887767585" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1887767585" />
    <a title="Eva Chau" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63090851-eva-chau"><img alt="Eva Chau" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590527075p2/63090851.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1887767585?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eva Chau" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eva Chau" href="/user/show/63090851-eva-chau">Eva Chau</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Eva by: </span>
      Booktasters
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1887767585" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18374698283763136530">What can I say about this story?<br/><br/>The Last Valentine is a story like none I’ve read. It’s different in a way of having more narration than I’m used to, but beautiful neither the less.<br/><br/>It’s a story you will fall in love for, a story you will read with a full heart and crave every word of it.<br/>It has mystery, secrecy and passion. It’s incredible to read the characters’ love stories and see how they all connect. When in a time people were not able to be with the person they pleased and loved, the Labyri</span>
  <span id="freeText18374698283763136530" style="display:none">What can I say about this story?<br /><br />The Last Valentine is a story like none I’ve read. It’s different in a way of having more narration than I’m used to, but beautiful neither the less.<br /><br />It’s a story you will fall in love for, a story you will read with a full heart and crave every word of it.<br />It has mystery, secrecy and passion. It’s incredible to read the characters’ love stories and see how they all connect. When in a time people were not able to be with the person they pleased and loved, the Labyrinth permitted them to see and fall in love with the person they were destined to be with, no matter who they were obligated to marry. <br /><br />Where forbidden love was more common and true love was something only a few could enjoy, this story will allow you to experience love in a way you have never experienced. You will feel the characters pain, for there is no love without pain (like The Last Valentine teaches us) or death, but also happiness and desire.<br /><br />The novel is very well written and its description of the places will make you travel there, like any good book you will be drawn into its world and your mind will be completely oblivious of what is happening around you, the only thing you will see and think about is Old Sienna. <br /><br />Unfortunately love and passion is not the only thing you will see, you will also witness greed and pride. Money and status are the things a lot of the men only cared about in that age. People will try to suppress other’s feelings to prevent their blood and heritage from being “corrupted”; they will do everything in their power to make sure they keep their appearances. It’s truly sad to see how some people can behave in order to feel powerful.<br /><br />The book will make you long for that kind of love, the kind that is overwhelming but you wouldn’t trade for anything. I believe we can have more than one true love, but if we are lucky enough to find it we should cherish it. Even though we might have the luck to experience another love we will ever forget the first one; as The Last Valentine tells us “Love is the only memory one never loses, because even if one loses his mind the memory always remains in the heart.”<br /><br />I thank Booktasters, on twitter, for introducing me to this wonderful book and Felix Alexander for writing it.<br /><br />A book I will re-read anytime I want to feel the deep love that brought me to tears at the end. A book I recommend any romantic to read.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18374698283763136530" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1865335031" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1865335031" />
    <a title="Wulfwyn " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2288988-wulfwyn"><img alt="Wulfwyn " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1241549192p2/2288988.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1865335031?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wulfwyn " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wulfwyn " href="/user/show/2288988-wulfwyn">Wulfwyn </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1865335031" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2500057197846517052">I love the writing in this book! This is a book for the true romantic. The author writes with a poetic hand. I thought it was atmospheric and haunting. Oddly I felt as if I were the ghost though. I was the one haunting the characters. I was transported to 1930's Puerto Rico and it was I drifting through scene after scene bearing witness to love found, love lost, love searched for, love longed for. I haunted the characters for their memories. I followed them in their search for the labyrinth. I h</span>
  <span id="freeText2500057197846517052" style="display:none">I love the writing in this book! This is a book for the true romantic. The author writes with a poetic hand. I thought it was atmospheric and haunting. Oddly I felt as if I were the ghost though. I was the one haunting the characters. I was transported to 1930's Puerto Rico and it was I drifting through scene after scene bearing witness to love found, love lost, love searched for, love longed for. I haunted the characters for their memories. I followed them in their search for the labyrinth. I hungered for all they offered and wanted more. If you choose to read this book, (if you are romantic you must!), make sure to set aside time undisturbed. <br />The pace of the book is slow. For me, that felt the right speed though others may disagree. Maybe it is the flow of language. Maybe it is my own perception that time moves slower in certain places or times and with certain circumstances. For whatever reason, I thought it moved perfectly with the story being told. I loved going back through the memories of the characters. If you are not use to reading stories written this way, the floating in and out of memories may be a bit confusing until you find your way. There is also not as much dialogue as other books have. I remember, at one point, thinking of the movie The Others. Not a great movie but the story and the atmosphere, I loved. I was also reminded of books I had read by Gabriel Garcia Marquez. This author has the same ability to make me feel that Marquez does. The only thing worth living for, and dying for, is love. Insert a huge sigh here. I sighed while reading. I sighed at the ending. I sigh upon remembering it. My heart yearns for this love that is worth everything. <br />I received an e copy of this book from the author through BookTasters. I was offered it to read. I voluntarily wrote a review. I especially try to write reviews for books I fell in love with. I want everyone to read those. This book is one I fell in love with. I hope you do to. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2500057197846517052" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49444196-katie-b?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2282811023" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8404524058942385394">In 1935, the corpse of an unidentified man is found in a darkened alley in Puerto Rico. Olivia, the daughter of a police investigator, finds a bloodstained love letter in her father's coat after he comes home drunk one night. She is convinced it came from the deceased man and teams up with her friend Issac to deliver it to the Labyrinth of Love Letters. The only problem is even though they have heard of this place where lovers leave notes for one another, they have no idea of its location. As th</span>
  <span id="freeText8404524058942385394" style="display:none">In 1935, the corpse of an unidentified man is found in a darkened alley in Puerto Rico. Olivia, the daughter of a police investigator, finds a bloodstained love letter in her father's coat after he comes home drunk one night. She is convinced it came from the deceased man and teams up with her friend Issac to deliver it to the Labyrinth of Love Letters. The only problem is even though they have heard of this place where lovers leave notes for one another, they have no idea of its location. As they set forth on a quest to bring the letter to its intended destination, they uncover secrets from long ago that will impact their lives forever. <br /><br />This book had a few too many characters and story lines to keep track of which made it hard for me to ever get in a good flow of reading. It's one of those things where because it is such an intricately detailed plot, it is confusing how all of these characters and their story lines fit together until the very end. This is probably a book I would enjoy more on a second read.<br /><br /><i>The Last Valentine</i> is a unique story and really explores the topic of true love and the sacrifices people make because of it. I enjoyed the setting of Puerto Rico and loved the concept of the Labyrinth of Love Letters. I'd say give this book a shot if you are interested in something a bit more dark and mysterious in the romance genre.<br /><br />I won a free copy of this ebook in a giveaway but was under no obligation to post a review. All views expressed are my honest opinion. </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1872424310" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer324208112759860857">The Last Valentine A Labyrinth of Love Letters Novel by Felix Alexander is a story of romance and mystery set in 1935 Puerto Rico. The story follows Olivia Villalobos, the daughter of a police investigator. She comes across a bloodstained love letter in her father's coat. The letter peeks Olivia's interest. She wonders why her father would have the letter in his possession and if it's connected to an unsolved murder that recently happened. She shares her discovery with her best friend Issac who </span>
  <span id="freeText324208112759860857" style="display:none">The Last Valentine A Labyrinth of Love Letters Novel by Felix Alexander is a story of romance and mystery set in 1935 Puerto Rico. The story follows Olivia Villalobos, the daughter of a police investigator. She comes across a bloodstained love letter in her father's coat. The letter peeks Olivia's interest. She wonders why her father would have the letter in his possession and if it's connected to an unsolved murder that recently happened. She shares her discovery with her best friend Issac who thinks they should turn the letter in to the police, but Olivia is determined to find the Labyrinth of Love Letters so the intended recipient can receive her letter. The Labyrinth of Love Letters according to local legends is a series of tunnels underneath the city of Old Sienna where lovers could express their secrets to their lovers through letters and hide them in the tunnels. Many people believe is just a legend and that it does it exist, but Olivia and Isaac set out to find the Labyrinth. Upon their journey of discovery they come across stories of forbidden love and arranged marriages, lies and deception among the aristocrats, and the the extent to which the powerful wish to keep the their secrets buried. <br />I recommend this book. Especially if you are a fan of Gabriel Garcia Marquez. This book definitely reminded me of his work. The story is beautifully written. I enjoyed the mixture of romance, mystery and historical fiction in the setting of Puerto Rico. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3817450606270669299">*Received via BookTasters in exchange for an honest review. The thoughts are entirely my own and in no way biased.*<br/><br/>First of, I love the premise of this story! A love letter in possession of the murder victim and just about the only clue the police has to catch the killer. And to top it, it's set in earlier times. I'm sort of a history buff and I didn't know much about Old Sienna or Peurto Rico in 1935, so I like that too! It's murder and mystery and romance and awesome!<br/><br/>I love the writing style. </span>
  <span id="freeText3817450606270669299" style="display:none">*Received via BookTasters in exchange for an honest review. The thoughts are entirely my own and in no way biased.*<br /><br />First of, I love the premise of this story! A love letter in possession of the murder victim and just about the only clue the police has to catch the killer. And to top it, it's set in earlier times. I'm sort of a history buff and I didn't know much about Old Sienna or Peurto Rico in 1935, so I like that too! It's murder and mystery and romance and awesome!<br /><br />I love the writing style. It is amazing and beautiful and lyrical and JUST SO FREAKING SHIZ GOOD THAT YOU CAN'T HELP BUT LOVE IT! I loved the setting, the plot and the writing of this novel so much. There is so much speculation and conjecture and intrigue. Also, there's this amazing romance. So, what's not to like?<br /><br />The major issue I had with this book was despite all it's good points, I couldn't find myself getting attached to the characters. I wasn't rooting for anyone and I didn't connect with them as well as I was hoping to, which put a damper on all the nice things about it. <br /><br />But, hey! That's just me. I'm sure that all romance and mystery fans will find this book enjoyable!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3817450606270669299" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15756612763828007378">This has to be the most unique love and mystery book I have ever had the pleasure of reading. This story weaves several love stories together within it using a single love letter that is part of a murder investigation. I love how the passing of the letter brings forth a new tragic love story for each character and how there is also a mystery linked to it.   <span id="freeText15756612763828007378" style="display:none">This has to be the most unique love and mystery book I have ever had the pleasure of reading. This story weaves several love stories together within it using a single love letter that is part of a murder investigation. I love how the passing of the letter brings forth a new tragic love story for each character and how there is also a mystery linked to it. The author is also great with putting historical elements together. the story is set in the mid 1930s, and the roles of both men and women at the time are realistic as well as the settings and dialogue. You can imagine all these people in smoky bar rooms and lounges that are missing from modern society with quite that same film noire feel. If you get the chance, read this, because you won't be bored at all.</span>

<div id="review_1813771245" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1813771245" />
    <a title="Elizabeth Mathis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27262917-elizabeth-mathis"><img alt="Elizabeth Mathis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479071720p2/27262917.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1813771245?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth Mathis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth Mathis" href="/user/show/27262917-elizabeth-mathis">Elizabeth Mathis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27262917-elizabeth-mathis?shelf=reviewed-contemporary">reviewed-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27262917-elizabeth-mathis?shelf=reviewed-historical">reviewed-historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27262917-elizabeth-mathis?shelf=reviewed-romance">reviewed-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1813771245" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16352282816187030560"><blockquote>When Olivia Villalobos finds a bloodstained love letter she endeavors to deliver it before Chief Inspector Sedeño finds it in her possession.<br/><br/>A city along the southern coast of Puerto Rico emerges in the aftermath of the Spanish-American War. Olivia, daughter of a drunkard police investigator who never knew the truth behind her mother’s disappearance, finds a bloodstained love letter in the hidden compartment of her father’s coat. Convinced it belonged to the man recently found dead she sets out </blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText16352282816187030560" style="display:none"><blockquote>When Olivia Villalobos finds a bloodstained love letter she endeavors to deliver it before Chief Inspector Sedeño finds it in her possession.<br /><br />A city along the southern coast of Puerto Rico emerges in the aftermath of the Spanish-American War. Olivia, daughter of a drunkard police investigator who never knew the truth behind her mother’s disappearance, finds a bloodstained love letter in the hidden compartment of her father’s coat. Convinced it belonged to the man recently found dead she sets out to deliver it to the Labyrinth of Love Letters. A mysterious place believed to be an urban legend where the transients of forbidden love leave missives for one another. She enlists the help of Isaac Quintero to find the Labyrinth and they soon realize their quest has opened the door into Old Sienna’s darkest secrets—the perils, madness and depth of tragic love</blockquote><br /><br /><b>Rating: 3.5/5 Penguins<br />Quick Reasons: lots of purple prose and beautiful descriptions; there wasn't much "plot" to this story; cliched, too-clean ending; I didn't really connect with any of these characters, though I did empathize with a few; overall entertaining, question-evoking, and complex read</b><br /><br />Huge thanks to Felix Alexander and <a href="https://twitter.com/BookTasters" rel="nofollow noopener">BookTasters</a> for sending me a free digital ARC of this title in exchange for an honest review! This in no way altered my read of or opinions on this book.<br /><br /><blockquote> "Where are you off to in such a hurry?" Uncle Gabriel asked as he sat on one of his patio chairs.<br /><br />"We're off to find the secrets of the Romantics," Olivia said over her shoulder.<br /><br />"Be careful nena, for the Romantics are a dark breed and their secrets are even darker than the valleys of their souls." </blockquote><br /><br />First things first: this was an interesting, though not necessarily action-packed, read. What I mean is, I was super intrigued and held in pretty deep thrall...but I feel as if certain parts of this might have moved a bit slowly, all together. A lot of this book is internal monologues and ponderments; there is not overall a lot of dialogue. Which I suppose, in a sense, makes sense--these characters are, for all intents and purposes, romantics in their own rights...and therefore given to being lost in their own heads. But it does not, in the end, lend itself to action scenes or quite the right "mood" for what is meant. This read much more like an overreaching love-story, not what turned out to be a sort of murder/mystery.<br /><br />The characters are intriguing and complex, but I didn't find myself really "connecting" with any of them. Yes, I was able to empathize with and understand their motives...but I found I didn't really care for them in the end. I wasn't rooting for them, or holding my breath in anticipation, or fearing for their safety. I was sort of a neutral ground in the scope of this read--not really swayed or moved by the course of events. Even the characters who were meant to be HUGE in personality, fell a bit flat for me, unfortunately.<br /><br /><blockquote> "Love is a potion, and many ingredients are used to enhance its potency, or alter the flavor. Infatuation makes it sweet, longing makes it strong, and agony makes it bitter. But desire is poisonous because it leads one to confuse lust for love, which always leads to heartbreak." </blockquote><br /><br />I REALLY enjoyed the purple prose aspect, though. Seeing as Felix Alexander is a poet, I went into this read expecting gorgeous scene-setting and beautiful descriptors, and I was not disappointed in either of these aspects. The scenery, the world, the sounds and tastes--everything leaped to life around me as I read, helping to better "immerse" me in the book. Felix Alexander did a beautiful job painting this world for me. <br /><br />I was, in the end, a bit disappointed with the ending. While I understand why it was done the way it is, it's also...very cliche? in books like this, I feel--and in movies, as well. It also sort of took me by surprise, as I hadn't seen that ending coming quite as soon as it did (or, it felt soon to me, given the way the characters had been described). <br /><br />This was an enjoyably descriptive, though a bit plot-slow, read. I had a ton of fun following Olivia and Isaac on their journey; I had more fun being immersed in and awed by the scenery and world being built. I recommend this to lovers of old-world secrets, the consequences of forbidden love affairs, and murder/mysteries that feel more like long-winded romances. Felix Alexander penned a love letter around his readers; why don't you pick it up and read?</span>
  <a data-text-id="16352282816187030560" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2223355009?book_show_action=true">Dec 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jewel Hart" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jewel Hart" href="/user/show/56470711-jewel-hart">Jewel Hart</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2223355009" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer705018223908874198">The Last Valentine by Felix Alexander is a sweeping epic saga of multiple love stories within one story.<br/><br/>It is filled with poetic beauty that captures the soul. The scenery and descriptions are penned so beautifully that the vivid scenes come alive in the reader’s mind. Skillfully written in lyrical poetic beauty, The Last Valentine is a treat to be savored. The words flow beautifully straight off the page.<br/><br/>The storyline is unique and very different in that it involves many generations of love sto</span>
  <span id="freeText705018223908874198" style="display:none">The Last Valentine by Felix Alexander is a sweeping epic saga of multiple love stories within one story.<br /><br />It is filled with poetic beauty that captures the soul. The scenery and descriptions are penned so beautifully that the vivid scenes come alive in the reader’s mind. Skillfully written in lyrical poetic beauty, The Last Valentine is a treat to be savored. The words flow beautifully straight off the page.<br /><br />The storyline is unique and very different in that it involves many generations of love stories and unrequited love. I was captivated by Felix Alexander’s words and imagination. The plot is rich and fulfilling.<br /><br />The many characters are fully developed and multi-dimensional. The author really put a lot into developing, not only the storyline, but the eccentric characters as well.<br /><br />This novel will take readers away to a different time and place where romance is the main theme.<br /><br />It’s not like a typical chick lit style read or even a contemporary romance. This is more like the writings of some of the great romantic drama writers of all time.<br /><br />I fell in love with The Last Valentine and couldn’t put it down, reading into the late hours of the night.<br /><br />This is a compelling engaging read that I recommend to true literary readers which crave good old fashioned classic romance poetry and stories.<br /><br />Compelling and beautiful, The Last Valentine is engaging and written with expertise.<br /><br />This story is for real true romantics, there is a lot of mystery and disturbing twists which adds to the overall greatness of the novel. The satisfying ending is smooth and welcomed.<br /><br />I truly loved The Last Valentine and would read it again-for unrequited love is the most heartbreaking love of all.</span>

<div id="review_2037974359" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2037974359" />
    <a title="Virginia Marks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45701696-virginia-marks"><img alt="Virginia Marks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494455344p2/45701696.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2037974359?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Marks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Marks" href="/user/show/45701696-virginia-marks">Virginia Marks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2037974359" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15944662627189780193">As any romance story goes, you know that there must be a trial to test the strength of the love. Even in Puerto Rico has the same woes as the rest of the world.<br/><br/>Lorenzo Valentino was the equivalent of Romeo and Juliet. He fell in love with a woman who was poor and forbidden. It didn't matter to him, he was in love and he was going to prove it. He attained information of a secret tunnel below the city that had many ways to enter. He knew that if they were going to keep their relationship a secret,</span>
  <span id="freeText15944662627189780193" style="display:none">As any romance story goes, you know that there must be a trial to test the strength of the love. Even in Puerto Rico has the same woes as the rest of the world.<br /><br />Lorenzo Valentino was the equivalent of Romeo and Juliet. He fell in love with a woman who was poor and forbidden. It didn't matter to him, he was in love and he was going to prove it. He attained information of a secret tunnel below the city that had many ways to enter. He knew that if they were going to keep their relationship a secret, he must come up with a plan. So he closed off all entries except for one. He would write love letters and have secret meetings inside the walls. His love didn't last when his father decided against her. Some say that his father killed his son so to hide the shame. Other people believed that he killed himself when his lover left. Whatever the reason the tunnel now was in his memory and the sacredness of love would be forever protected. Thus he became known as The Lost Valentine.<br /><br />Forward many years to 1935 at the scene of a gruesome murder a love letter was found. No identification was on the body nor was there any information about the creater of the love letter. When the letter came up missing from the police evidence room it set a series of events that some call chance and others call it destiny.<br /><br />Chief Inspector Guillerno Sedeno fell in love with a woman and was crushed when she was forced to marry another man. Politics played a major part in relationships back then. Instead of marrying for love people would marry to grew money or to keep old money in the family. Now he is alone and working as the Chief kept him busy. When the letter came up missing he knew the first place to look.<br /><br />Javier Villalobos in an Inspector with an immense reputation with his name as well as his police work. Ever since his wife went missing (the Chief's love) he has found the only solace he could find was in the bottle of the bottle. He was left with a screaming daughter and called in his sister to raise his daughter. Everyone swore that Olivia looked her mother, but two features must come from the ancestors instead of her father.<br /><br />Oliva is 17yrs old and when her drunken father passed out on his bed, she emptied out his coat and found a letter with dried blood. Giving into excitement and the thrist to right a wrong, she sets off with her best friend to find the Labrinth of Lovers. The path she finds has more questions than answers that she is not ready to hear. He best friend Isaac is willing to sacrifice his heart and love to find the Labrinth. Only someone with a person with real relationship problems could ever find or use the Labrinth. Many swear that it is a legend. In this story there are many twists and turns in the search for truth. Someone's life will ruined with more than just a rumor of infidelity. <br /><br />The romance part of this story is very interesting and pulls the readers inside and won't let them go. The story has a great flow of understanding the culture as well. Somewhere in the midst of this story you find that there are more things in a rose garden than just flowers. I love how the history was used in this story as a way to draw the reader into the web. It made me hope for the lovers and to be grateful for never having to feel that kind of pain.<br /><br />This book is great for young adults since there is only one sex scene and it is very quick (pun not intended)! I was given this book to review from the author/publisher through Reading Alley and in exchange I give my unbiased opinion.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15944662627189780193" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1819857220" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1819857220" />
    <a title="Caroline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13405236-caroline"><img alt="Caroline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479935534p2/13405236.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1819857220?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caroline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caroline" href="/user/show/13405236-caroline">Caroline</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13405236-caroline?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1819857220" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6949532840234569624">I received an advance copy of this book in exchange for an honest review. <br/><br/>The Last Valentine is set in Puerto Rico near the start of the Twentieth Century. An unidentified man is murdered, a letter he was carrying the only clue to his identity. The letter goes missing from the police station and Olivia, daughter of an alcoholic policeman, discovers it in her father's coat. She realises it is a letter declaring undying but forbidden love and resolves to find the semi-mythical Labyrinth of Love Le</span>
  <span id="freeText6949532840234569624" style="display:none">I received an advance copy of this book in exchange for an honest review. <br /><br />The Last Valentine is set in Puerto Rico near the start of the Twentieth Century. An unidentified man is murdered, a letter he was carrying the only clue to his identity. The letter goes missing from the police station and Olivia, daughter of an alcoholic policeman, discovers it in her father's coat. She realises it is a letter declaring undying but forbidden love and resolves to find the semi-mythical Labyrinth of Love Letters with the help of her friend Isaac, so she can deliver it to its rightful recipient. The Labyrinth is a place for lovers who can't be together to communicate, pouring out their passions into love letters, left for each other in their own special place. Throughout the story, we meet a myriad of characters, all with secrets, loves and desires of their own, some of them users of this secret labyrinth. I found this story intriguing and compelling: it has a touch of the supernatural and consequently creates a similar atmosphere to other magical realist authors, e.g. Garcia Marquez. I liked the fact that it wasn't a simple love story, but more of a story about the nature of love. Political intrigue and corruption was built into the plot, making it exciting towards the end. There were some lovely descriptive phrases, e.g. 'a shadow among shadows, a freshly minted phantom of unrequited love'. The language itself was romantic and heartfelt, creating a place where passionate love is the most important part of life, but the dictates of society mean that it cannot always be acted upon.<br /><br />I have a few minor gripes: it could do with some spelling and grammar checks: commas were missing in places and there were misspellings, e.g. steak-out rather than stake-out, mostly ones that would have been missed by a computer spellchecker. There were bits of description that were a little repetitive: there's a section in the middle where everyone does everything 'pensively'. There was also a little too much background explanation for me for some of the references: I'd prefer just a poet's name if a character is quoting them and I'll look them up myself if I want more information. I think the explanations broke up the flow of the text. <br />Ultimately it was a great story, just needs a bit of polishing, so it deserves a 4*.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6949532840234569624" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1834765238" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1834765238" />
    <a title="R.J. Groves" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/61941118-r-j-groves"><img alt="R.J. Groves" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588832258p2/61941118.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1834765238?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="R.J. Groves" class="user" itemprop="url" name="R.J. Groves" href="/user/show/61941118-r-j-groves">R.J. Groves</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1834765238" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12346997712928480802">Set in Puerto Rico in the year 1935, "The Last Valentine" tells a story of forbidden love and the search for the mythical (or so it was considered) Labyrinth of Love Letters. After the death of a mystery man, a bloodstained letter - the only clue to the man's identity - finds its way into Olivia Villalobos' possession. Instead of giving the letter back to the police, Olivia begins her search for the Labyrinth of Love Letters with her best friend, Isaac, to ensure that the intended recipient of t</span>
  <span id="freeText12346997712928480802" style="display:none">Set in Puerto Rico in the year 1935, "The Last Valentine" tells a story of forbidden love and the search for the mythical (or so it was considered) Labyrinth of Love Letters. After the death of a mystery man, a bloodstained letter - the only clue to the man's identity - finds its way into Olivia Villalobos' possession. Instead of giving the letter back to the police, Olivia begins her search for the Labyrinth of Love Letters with her best friend, Isaac, to ensure that the intended recipient of the letter receives it. Little did they know that they walked into a Pandora's box of corruption and mystery. <br /><br />I received an advanced review copy from the author for an honest opinion. <br /><br />I found the storyline intriguing and interesting - I was hooked from the start, wanting to know how it would all pan out. Felix Alexander set very descriptive scenes in a way that only a poet could. His descriptions were able to successfully paint a picture in my mind of the scenes. Though, I feel there wasn't enough dialogue in the story - some of the descriptions could have been changed to dialogue (especially ones talking about the past) and it would have helped the story flow better. I was invested in the story, but I would have liked to connect more with the characters and see the blossoming romances some more. There was a lot of looking into the past (memories etc) that sometimes interrupted the flow of the story because it was difficult to tell when it was talking about the present again. But once I got used to the style of writing, it became easier to determine the difference.<br /><br />Overall, it was a good read and I would recommend it to anyone looking for a romance story that would stand out. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12346997712928480802" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1857675122?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsey" href="/user/show/50338441-lindsey">Lindsey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1857675122" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5093799804166313618">I got a copy of this from Booktasters for an honest review.<br/><br/>So, the Last Valentine is more of a story about love and romantics than it is a love story. There's a lot of philosophizing, inner monologues, and backstories. There is not a lot of dialogue or character development. Sometimes the story is hard to follow because it starts and stops for flashbacks. The story could be organized a little differently to flow more smoothly and be more evenly paced. I think, actually, it might make a cool shor</span>
  <span id="freeText5093799804166313618" style="display:none">I got a copy of this from Booktasters for an honest review.<br /><br />So, the Last Valentine is more of a story about love and romantics than it is a love story. There's a lot of philosophizing, inner monologues, and backstories. There is not a lot of dialogue or character development. Sometimes the story is hard to follow because it starts and stops for flashbacks. The story could be organized a little differently to flow more smoothly and be more evenly paced. I think, actually, it might make a cool short film, even if the ending is a little bit cliche and expected.<br /><br />I'm not sure if this is a finished copy, but there were quite a few typos and errors. At times it was distracting and Alexander could benefit from a copyeditor. There are some beautiful lines, but at times some of it was overdone prose. <br /><br />I love the set up- a bloodstained love letter on a murder victim? In historic Puerto Rico? What's a better setting for a story? Unfortunately, I found it a little slow from there, although the *idea* of the plot is cool. I wish there was more character development, they kind of feel like plot devices and not actual people. <br /><br />If you like philosophy and intrigue and a little mystery, this may be the book for you. 2.5-3 stars. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5093799804166313618" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13110465183341804265">*Disclaimer: I recieved a free copy of this book via Booktasters and the author*<br/><br/>I really enjoyed reading this. Felix Alexander writes beautifully. I'm not the biggest fan of romance--but this book had such beautiful prose that it was easy to keep reading. However, at times, it does seem a bit too descriptive.<br/><br/>It's easy to feel like you've been transported to 1930s Puerto Rico with the way Alexander writes. The storyline--which features more than just romance--is intriguing and helps the reader st</span>
  <span id="freeText13110465183341804265" style="display:none">*Disclaimer: I recieved a free copy of this book via Booktasters and the author*<br /><br />I really enjoyed reading this. Felix Alexander writes beautifully. I'm not the biggest fan of romance--but this book had such beautiful prose that it was easy to keep reading. However, at times, it does seem a bit too descriptive.<br /><br />It's easy to feel like you've been transported to 1930s Puerto Rico with the way Alexander writes. The storyline--which features more than just romance--is intriguing and helps the reader stay hooked despite the excessive description. Be cautious of not noticing that certain parts of the novel are memories, otherwise you might get a little confused when it breaks up the story's flow. There isn't much dialogue, which makes it hard to feel like you've connected to the characters.<br /><br />My advanced copy had some typos, which I hope are caught before publication. Otherwise, I highly recommend this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13110465183341804265" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2038361162" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2038361162" />
    <a title="Deanna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20102247-deanna"><img alt="Deanna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1367868224p2/20102247.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2038361162?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deanna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deanna" href="/user/show/20102247-deanna">Deanna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20102247-deanna?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2038361162" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3552218616041250439">I became Mr. Alexander’s newest fan with this book. This is an enchanting story of many loves, betrayal, mystery, murder, scandal, and, lessons in life, history, and, the arts.<br/>The story is set in Puerto Rico, with the main characters being in the 1930’s. The author describes many historical facts, as well as a detailed description of the beautiful settings and decor. Felix Alexander also displays a charming sense of humor throughout the book.<br/>The story centers around two children, their lives and</span>
  <span id="freeText3552218616041250439" style="display:none">I became Mr. Alexander’s newest fan with this book. This is an enchanting story of many loves, betrayal, mystery, murder, scandal, and, lessons in life, history, and, the arts.<br />The story is set in Puerto Rico, with the main characters being in the 1930’s. The author describes many historical facts, as well as a detailed description of the beautiful settings and decor. Felix Alexander also displays a charming sense of humor throughout the book.<br />The story centers around two children, their lives and loves--together and apart--and, secrets that they discover, along with their determination to find answers and resolve. <br />The drama is captivating. I read it in one sitting. The suspense held me fast to the very last word of the book. In fact, I was drawn in with the first paragraph. This is a story of romantic love--real love. It is neither sleazy, or, cheesy--unlike too many romance novels.<br />The only drawback is an apparent lack of proper editing. There are a few grammatical errors, and, a need for much more punctuation. Those are my only complaints. If you can overlook those, you should love this wonderful story.<br />Here are some of my favorite quotes from the book:<br /><br />"For love is not measured by a beginning and an end but rather by the depth of its sorrow and the height of its passion."<br /><br />"...love keeps us young after youth has passed and is the only memory worth remembering when the shadows of forgetfulness linger on the horizon of old age."<br /><br />“We never know our journey before it begins, but in hindsight we discover that every experience we have is meant to be ours and ours alone.”<br /><br /><br />"They passed through the stages of life without seeing in each other the changes that come with old age, for as they wrote their love story they fell deeper in love with the turn of every page."</span>
  <a data-text-id="3552218616041250439" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2060017001" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2060017001" />
    <a title="Angelica McDonald" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18490740-angelica-mcdonald"><img alt="Angelica McDonald" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1515027991p2/18490740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2060017001?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angelica McDonald" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angelica McDonald" href="/user/show/18490740-angelica-mcdonald">Angelica McDonald</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18490740-angelica-mcdonald?shelf=blog-review">blog-review</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2060017001" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7210508339884996266">Even though I truly loved this story, I did find myself confused at certain parts of the novel. For example, you may be reading from person’s point-of-view and then it will switch without warning to another’s. That part did irritate me at some moments so that is why I didn’t give this book a 5/5. That also seemed to happen with some settings in the novel too, but if it wasn’t for the author’s brilliant storytelling I would have given up on the novel because of that. Also, some of the grammar in </span>
  <span id="freeText7210508339884996266" style="display:none">Even though I truly loved this story, I did find myself confused at certain parts of the novel. For example, you may be reading from person’s point-of-view and then it will switch without warning to another’s. That part did irritate me at some moments so that is why I didn’t give this book a 5/5. That also seemed to happen with some settings in the novel too, but if it wasn’t for the author’s brilliant storytelling I would have given up on the novel because of that. Also, some of the grammar in the novel was off because of the lack of quotation marks and misspellings. I did think that the lack of quotation marks was just the style of writing the author used but I later discovered it was inconsistent.<br /><br />However, I would recommend this novel because it was beautifully written and it has been a while since I read something with such a lovely writing style. The author does have a unique talent.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7210508339884996266" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
