<div id="review_2039666937" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2039666937" />
    <a title="Caitlin Farley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29628360-caitlin-farley"><img alt="Caitlin Farley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1436684941p2/29628360.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2039666937?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caitlin Farley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caitlin Farley" href="/user/show/29628360-caitlin-farley">Caitlin Farley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2039666937" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2177601918275272343">The Labyrinth of Love Letters is just one of many secrets in the Puerto Rican city of Old Sienna. When Olivia finds a bloodstained love letter in her father’s coat, she becomes entranced by the poetic longing scribed on the page. She resolves to place the letter in the legendary Labyrinth of Love Letters. Even the discovery that the letter is a stolen piece of evidence in the unsolved murder of an unidentified man does not deter her from her goal. Olivia convinces her close friend, Isaac, to hel</span>
  <span id="freeText2177601918275272343" style="display:none">The Labyrinth of Love Letters is just one of many secrets in the Puerto Rican city of Old Sienna. When Olivia finds a bloodstained love letter in her father’s coat, she becomes entranced by the poetic longing scribed on the page. She resolves to place the letter in the legendary Labyrinth of Love Letters. Even the discovery that the letter is a stolen piece of evidence in the unsolved murder of an unidentified man does not deter her from her goal. Olivia convinces her close friend, Isaac, to help her. Little do the pair know that some of the Labyrinth’s secrets are deeper and darker than the letters exchanged between forbidden lovers. One of those secrets would mean death for Olivia if she were ever to discover it. <br /><br />The Last Valentine is a novel of romantic love in all its forms, from happy ever afters and the loneliness of unrequited love, to the tragedy of impossible, secret romances confined to whispers and the cover of darkness. There were times when I thought it was glorifying the unhealthy side of romance a bit much, but it works in the context and fits the theme. Felix Alexander’s writing is poetic and evokes a great sense of mood throughout. This is accentuated and refined by its 30s setting and the classist attitudes of this era. The characters all intertwine and connect with each other, often in ways I didn’t anticipate, and their motives direct the plot down a path littered with deep, dark secrets.<br /><br />(Reviewed for Reader's Favorite)</span>
  <a data-text-id="2177601918275272343" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2007431141" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2007431141" />
    <a title="A.C. Cole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59855691-a-c-cole"><img alt="A.C. Cole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474470959p2/59855691.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2007431141?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="A.C. Cole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="A.C. Cole" href="/user/show/59855691-a-c-cole">A.C. Cole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59855691-a-c-cole?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2007431141&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2007431141" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14814016554122202527">I thoroughly enjoyed this novel from start to finish. This is one is for the romantics, although there is a mysterious and sinister twist to it all. The words flow right off the page and I found myself highlighting lengthy portions to revisit later. My review contains a lot of spoilers, so beware! <br/><br/>This was my first experience with Mr. Alexander’s work, so I was not familiar with his writing style. When I stated the words flow, I truly mean that. The beginning chapters of this book are introducti</span>
  <span id="freeText14814016554122202527" style="display:none">I thoroughly enjoyed this novel from start to finish. This is one is for the romantics, although there is a mysterious and sinister twist to it all. The words flow right off the page and I found myself highlighting lengthy portions to revisit later. My review contains a lot of spoilers, so beware! <br /><br />This was my first experience with Mr. Alexander’s work, so I was not familiar with his writing style. When I stated the words flow, I truly mean that. The beginning chapters of this book are introductions to character after character. It begins with one, who encounters the next, and then the next, and so on. Each time, you’re given an overview of the person including a curtailed back story and pertinent current information. I stopped after the sixth chapter and thought to myself…I think I just met fifty people (an exaggeration) and I know a good bit about each of them. And yet, I was not confused. Each one stood out as an individual distinct from all the others.  Nor was I confused for the rest of the novel. It was easy to understand who was who. When I stopped to think about it, there was an overload of information. However, it did not seem like it at all. Mr. Alexander created a flow with the story that was a natural transition from character to character. Weirdly, I was interested in all of them. I sympathized with some more than others, but I was genuinely interested in what happened to these people.<br />There is a large cast of characters. While their relationships are stated clearly at the beginning, it was interesting to see how they evolved over the course of the novel. Some are more than they seem and unraveling the mystery as fun. Who exactly is the last Valentine? The book centers around Isaac more than I realized it would based on the description. I was pleasantly surprised because, while Olivia is at the heart of the novel, seeing the action through Isaac’s eyes brought the story an entirely different feel. I’ll admit I was slightly more captivated by Isaac’s fate than I was by Olivia’s.  They are intertwined and yet separate at the same time. A diverting notion.<br />While this book is full of love, it is also full of tragedy and sorrow.<br />“Isaac contemplated the analogous nature of love and war and wondered if it true that nothing is the same after war and nothing is the same after love.”<br />True, no?<br />There are moments of levity, though they are minimal. Uncle Gabriel is a fascinating character that I would very much like to share a drink with.<br />“Uncle Gabriel shrugged. ‘Though I never pay much attention to what people say. Most people have no idea what they’re talking about anyway.'”<br />I laughed out loud at this part.<br />The novel is set in 1930s Puerto Rico. I have very little knowledge of this time period or place, however Mr. Alexander did a great job setting the scene. The necessary historical background was given smoothly. While some characters (Olivia and Isaac) move freely about the town, others are generally only seen in their own residences. For people like Uncle Gabriel, Umberto, the Mad Hatter, and the Elder Valentine, their homes seemed to be molded to the characteristics of their personalities. They inhabit these spaces and the spaces are them. The setting compliments them and brings out the essence of their characters.<br />There are no cliffhangers in this book. The ends are tied tightly. While some could argue it is too clean, I disagree. Love is messy. It is throughout the book and will be after the characters take their final breaths. Knowing the final fate for every character does not take away from that. For me, this novel made me think beyond the characters. It took me much longer to finish this because I would stop reading to contemplate particular passages. While the book could be viewed as a commentary on love, it is different for each reader. It is a compelling piece of literature that can make you think about questions beyond those posed on the page. I like books that I can take with me or that take parts of me with them. This was one of those for me.<br />First Thought When Finishing the Novel:<br />Isaac’s children make me sad.<br />Final Thought:<br />“It was a long, deep kiss. The kind that led the ancients to believe an exchange of souls occurred. Mauricio felt his heart drop.” I loved this line. A thousand emotions and thoughts opened up. I noted so many quotes from this novel that I cannot possibly put them all in this blog post. This novel was thought-provoking for me. I enjoyed it. I loved it. I’ll read it again.<br />Notes:<br />I received a free digital copy of this book in exchange for an honest review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14814016554122202527" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('tT5B+HaeAevz4lFfcjgYylmiGSHI+nF4I2QM7KDFgqNfATc4LTVFVFDyX1JbECAil9QG2sYIjULVa8NrrqRxIA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5btv4gbyGmtFpk7zQXGiMbScmsiN+Cp5sR/27FCbuZ8PhBkiXVle1Oa2QP5oWZrZeuqFM4MK1kNHEDlrXvpKHA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8375864595388718870">Felix Alexander (1976-Present) is a Mexican-born, American-raised novelist, and poet of Mexican and Puerto Rican descent.<br/><br/>Acclaimed by readers for his poetic prose, his indie releases include:<br/> <br/>* Dear Love: Diary of a Man's Desire, a collection of love letters and poems<br/>* The Romantic: A Love Story <br/>* Shadows of Time: The Amulet of Alamin<br/>* The Secret of Heaven (Book 1 of the Aiden Leonardo Series)<br/>*The</span>
  <span id="freeText8375864595388718870" style="display:none">Felix Alexander (1976-Present) is a Mexican-born, American-raised novelist, and poet of Mexican and Puerto Rican descent.<br /><br />Acclaimed by readers for his poetic prose, his indie releases include:<br /> <br />* Dear Love: Diary of a Man's Desire, a collection of love letters and poems<br />* The Romantic: A Love Story <br />* Shadows of Time: The Amulet of Alamin<br />* The Secret of Heaven (Book 1 of the Aiden Leonardo Series)<br />*The Secret of Scripture (Book 2 of the Aiden Leonardo Series)<br />*The Last Valentine (A Labyrinth of Love Letters novel)<br />*The Last Love Letter (A Labyrinth of Love Letters novel, book 2)<br />*Her Punishment (an erotic novelette)<br />*Her Awakening, an erotic romance novel<br />*A Uniquely Portable Magic, An Order of the Scribes adventure<br />*Romantic Musings, a collection of love letters and poems.<br /><br />Being third-generation military, after a grandfather and uncle who served in the Korean War and Vietnam War, respectively, Alexander is proud of his service in the U.S. Army, and grateful for his experience.<br /><br />After his honorable discharge from the U.S. Army, he embarked on the long and arduous journey of a writer. Having made a name for himself during his tenure, serving his country, he vowed to himself and his fellow soldiers that he would answer his true calling.<br /><br />He currently lives in Chicago, IL—to be closer to his children—a son and daughter. He volunteers to promote literacy among youth with Villament Charities and the VM Mag (vmmag.org).<br /><br />In the evenings he journeys through the portals of his extensive, personal library. When he returns, he immerses himself in his writing, and pursues the scent of his muse.</span>
